  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_262f8980-0278-42a1-a6fe-b7f70f1e4081'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText16455460175275842845" style="display:none">"My name is Sam. I am eleven years old. I collect stories and fantastic facts. Sam needs answers to the questions nobody will answer. "Ways To Live Forever" is the first novel from an extraordinarily talented young writer. Funny and honest, it is one of the most powerful and uplifting books you will ever read.</span>

<div id="review_87443760" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87443760" />
    <a title="Joe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/406752-joe"><img alt="Joe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497186280p2/406752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87443760?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe" href="/user/show/406752-joe">Joe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545069489" href="/book/show/3192561-ways-to-live-forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406752-joe?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406752-joe?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406752-joe?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406752-joe?shelf=this-stupid-book-made-me-cry">this-stupid-book-made-me-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87443760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15638220095948235112">Let's be honest. I usually only review books I can bash. It's something I like to do. But for <i>Ways to Live Forever</i>, one really must follow my thought process.<br/><br/><b>Page One Thoughts</b>: <i>This stupid book is going to make me cry.</i><br/><b>Page Seventy-Six Thoughts</b>: <i>Actually, this might turn out to be cheesy.</i><br/><b>Page One-Thirty-One Thoughts</b>: <i>Why am I scared of dying all of a sudden? Also, this is pretty heady stuff for young readers.</i><br/><b>Page One-Seventy-Two Thoughts</b>: <i>No! This is manipulative! This book wants me to cry! I wil</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15638220095948235112" style="display:none">Let's be honest. I usually only review books I can bash. It's something I like to do. But for <i>Ways to Live Forever</i>, one really must follow my thought process.<br /><br /><b>Page One Thoughts</b>: <i>This stupid book is going to make me cry.</i><br /><b>Page Seventy-Six Thoughts</b>: <i>Actually, this might turn out to be cheesy.</i><br /><b>Page One-Thirty-One Thoughts</b>: <i>Why am I scared of dying all of a sudden? Also, this is pretty heady stuff for young readers.</i><br /><b>Page One-Seventy-Two Thoughts</b>: <i>No! This is manipulative! This book wants me to cry! I will <u>not</u>!</i><br /><b>Page Two-Oh-Four</b>: <i>*uncontrollable sobbing*</i><br /><br />Make no mistake about it. Sally Nicholls could quite possibly be Nicholas Sparks for the middle school set. Her first novel, <i>Ways to Live Forever</i>, was written at the tender age of 23 and has all the trappings of youthful shmaltz: <br /><br />1. Sam is an eleven-year old with leukemia. He knows he's going to die. His <i>family</i> knows he's going to die. <i>
  <b>We</b>
</i> know he's going to die. There should be no surprises.<br /><br />2. Sam has an adorable sister, Ella, who is feisty and irrepressible. In other words, she's the stock little sister that populates every YA novel too lazy to create a real character.<br /><br />3. Sam's best friend is Felix, a sage in a wheelchair, also battling a terminal illness. Basic, unscrupulous foreshadowing.<br /><br />4. Sam makes a list of things to do before he dies. This is equivalent to Nicholls clicking her stopwatch and calling out, "Go!"<br /><br />5. Sam's handwriting, pictures, photos, and ticket stubs litter the book.... <i>like it's an actual scrapbook!!!</i><br /><br />Are you gagging yet?<br /><br />Don't. Because a Little Baby Jesus Christmas Miracle happens.<br /><br />Nicholls, for all her faults and reckless abandon, creates quite a lovely character in Sam. Although he's prone to thoughts that are a little out of sync with a kid his age, he is unusually grounded. Furthermore, his ruminations about death and dying are particularly child-like. This is the book's primary strength: in Sam, young readers will find a strong, likable boy who's been dealt a rotten hand. That Sam never feels sorry for himself, that he fights with his mother, that he is unapologetically stubborn are all the more meaningful as life slips from his fingertips.<br /><br />Perhaps even more astonishing is how Nicholls handles death. Throughout the books, she tosses off factoids about coffins, leukemia, and souls in a nearly insouciant manner. So disarming are these facts that several caused me to put the book aside and seriously consider my own death. Let's revisit that: A <i>children's</i> book caused me to think about my own death. Admittedly, this was embarrassingly anxiety-inducing at first, but being with Sam as he slowly dies eases that nervousness, if only because here's a kid, albeit a fictional one, who's facing the grim reaper with a savage bravery, and I'm getting upset about death. Man up, Joseph. <br /><br />So, yeah. There are some problems with <i>Ways to Live Forever</i>, but it's probably because of Nicholls' tender and impressionable age. But there's a good story squirreled away in the affectations, and it's a book many kids will quite enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15638220095948235112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16481629834852782022" style="display:none">"There's no point having wishes if you don't at least try to do them"<br /> <br /> —Sam McQueen, <i>Ways to Live Forever</i>, P. 60<br /><br /> This book subtly captured me and led me into its story, until before I even knew what was happening I was totally invested, heart, mind, and soul, in Sam and his life. The tension of approaching climax weighed on me as if it were happening to my own friend, and the panic juxtaposed against Sam's own calm regarding the seeming inevitability of his impending death lay powerfully on my mind the entire time. If this story were American, I would say that I could hardly think of another book winning the 2009 Newbery Medal.<br /><br /> "Things I Want to Happen After I die: You're allowed to be sad, but you're not allowed to be too sad. If you're always sad when you think about me, then how can you remember me?"<br /><br /> —Sam McQueen, <i>Ways to Live Forever</i>, P. 207</span>

<div id="review_1819933622" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1819933622" />
    <a title="Vivianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33012562-vivianne"><img alt="Vivianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580677327p2/33012562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1819933622?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivianne" href="/user/show/33012562-vivianne">Vivianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789026123603" href="/book/show/6462635-als-je-dit-leest-ben-ik-dood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012562-vivianne?shelf=z-4-stars">z-4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1819933622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15567812950429281112"><i>This book was so far out of my comfort zone..</i><br/><br/>This is a book you can read in one sitting and finish in about two hours. However I just couldn’t. I needed to be in the right mood for the final part because I knew what was coming.. So I put the book aside for like three months, and today was the day I picked it up again and broke my heart.<br/><br/>This book isn’t literature. It’s written very easily and it was really far out of my comfort zone because I normally read YA (dystopian/fantasy). But this book it</span>
  <span id="freeText15567812950429281112" style="display:none"><i>This book was so far out of my comfort zone..</i><br /><br />This is a book you can read in one sitting and finish in about two hours. However I just couldn’t. I needed to be in the right mood for the final part because I knew what was coming.. So I put the book aside for like three months, and today was the day I picked it up again and broke my heart.<br /><br />This book isn’t literature. It’s written very easily and it was really far out of my comfort zone because I normally read YA (dystopian/fantasy). But this book it shocked me awake, <i>it broke my heart and I’m still crying writing this review. </i><br /><br /><b>Sam is only ten years old and has cancer. He knows his days are limited so he decides to write a book about what he still wants to accomplice in life.</b> This book really reads like a diary and it is super quick and the beginning is actually quite fun. It really captures the life of a sick young child well, and it was so believable with all the sticky notes and lists. I actually learned a few new things from this book reading Sam’s fun facts. I also found the side characters, Sam’s family, Felix and Miss Wolters super believable. The dark side of this book was of course that Sam has cancer. <i>And there isn’t really any sugar coating the reality of a cancer patient.</i> But that actually was why this book was so heartbreaking. I know there are so many kids (and also adults) struggling with this disease. And I think that there isn’t a person walking this earth who doesn’t know someone who died off this terrible disease. And though you know what’s coming it doesn’t make it easier reading the final pages. I think I cried reading like the last 40 pages of this book. <br /><br />After I finished I sat there for about 10 minutes thinking about life with the book on my lap. It made me appreciate so many I have and take for granted. Being healthy and having a healthy family are one of the most important things in life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15567812950429281112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_47912453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

You can't often say that about what is supposed to be a kids' book, but this was so simply, heartbreakingly written, it was like ... it was so terrifically honest and convincing, half the time I was sure I was reading a true, Anne-Frank-style diary.   <span id="freeText1230443940775656345" style="display:none">This book is just... wow. I'm sorry I can't think of a more intelligent way to put it, but it was so incredibly ... beautiful. You can't often say that about what is supposed to be a kids' book, but this was so simply, heartbreakingly written, it was like ... it was so terrifically honest and convincing, half the time I was sure I was reading a true, Anne-Frank-style diary. Both Sam and Felix leapt off the page and in to my head, and I can tell you now, I will never forget them.<br />But what is so heartbreaking...there can never be a sequel. Although I think Ella is an interesting character. If she wanted, the author could explore her further in a companion book, although Ways to Live Forever is pretty stand-alone. It doesn't need a sequel. I just love Sam, is all. </span>

<div id="review_29850555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29850555" />
    <a title="Wezy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1415881-wezy"><img alt="Wezy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1218473070p2/1415881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29850555?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wezy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wezy" href="/user/show/1415881-wezy">Wezy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">If you like the children and dramatical books, it's a must read!!!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Wezy by: </span>
      No one at all
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29850555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14951758466286229898">When he was eight, the son of friends of mine went through a sort of John Webster phase, being much obsessed with death. His fondness for poking at road-kills and gazing at graveyards troubled his parents, of course, but not half as much as the interminable questions. What's it like to die? How do you know when you're dead? What happens afterwards? Why do we have to die anyway? These are "The Questions that Nobody Answers", according to Sam McQueen, the 11-year-old hero of Ways to Live Forever. </span>
  <span id="freeText14951758466286229898" style="display:none">When he was eight, the son of friends of mine went through a sort of John Webster phase, being much obsessed with death. His fondness for poking at road-kills and gazing at graveyards troubled his parents, of course, but not half as much as the interminable questions. What's it like to die? How do you know when you're dead? What happens afterwards? Why do we have to die anyway? These are "The Questions that Nobody Answers", according to Sam McQueen, the 11-year-old hero of Ways to Live Forever. But Sam isn't just going through his morbid phase. For him these questions have a special urgency because he is going to die, soon, and he knows it.<br /><br />Ways to Live Forever is the diary/scrapbook Sam compiles during the last two months of his life. Reading it is less like reading a novel than watching an exceptionally brilliant TV documentary. The text is punctuated by ephemera: drawings, tickets, and especially lists. Lists not only of those eternally unanswerable questions, but also of facts. Sam likes facts. He believes, touchingly, that they are the opposite of questions.<br /><br />A different kind of list gives the book its structure. "List No. 3: Things that I want to do" ranges from the entirely reasonable ("Go up down-escalators and go down up-escalators"), via the barely achievable ("Ride in an airship"), to the impossible ("Go up in a spaceship and see Earth from space"). I don't want to give away the plot, but I have to say that all these wishes are granted, one way or another.<br /><br />Killing children is something that writers indulge in from time to time. It's a high-risk business. If the crime is aggravated by mawkishness, the penalties can be severe. Passing sentence on Dickens, Oscar Wilde famously asserted that "One must have a heart of stone to read the death of Little Nell without laughing." In seeking to evade the charge of sentimentality, other writers have been sententious, offering pseudospiritual comforts, such as death being part of "a cycle" of some sort. (It is almost a rule, these days, that in children's literature death has to be presented as life-affirming, or even life-enhancing.) Beyond all this, of course, is the reasonable suspicion that killing children is the easiest way for writers to squeeze their readers' tear ducts. A surprising number of us think that a good cry is an essential part of a good read.<br /><br />Knowing all this, as she obviously does, Sally Nicholls has been either courageous or reckless to write, as her first novel, the story of a boy who dies of leukaemia. And she would seem to have made matters even more difficult for herself by writing in the first person, which means, among other things, that her narrator cannot be around to write the last scene. Does she get away with it? Yes, she does. She knows what the traps are, steps into them, and steps out again unscathed.<br /><br />In all first-person narratives the voice is, obviously, everything. Sam's is the voice of an unexceptional boy transformed by the enormity of what awaits him, and getting it to ring true is a hugely impressive achievement. I should mention (through gritted teeth) that Nicholls was only 23 when she wrote Ways to Live Forever. Her publishers have very high hopes for her, and on the strength of her debut they seem entirely justified. This is an elegant, intelligent, moving and sometimes even funny book. Young readers (and brave parents, and teachers) will love it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14951758466286229898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Meaghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/430758-meaghan"><img alt="Meaghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584945127p2/430758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meaghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meaghan" href="/user/show/430758-meaghan">Meaghan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545069489" href="/book/show/3192561-ways-to-live-forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/430758-meaghan?shelf=childrens-young-adult-fiction">childrens-young-adult-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183281238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2039846109968791496">The 9-to-12 age group's answer to Jenny Downham's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1314332.Before_I_Die' title='Before I Die by Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>Before I Die</a>. 11-year-old Sam keeps a notebook in the final months of his life, while he's getting palliative care for his leukemia. He's on homebound instruction with his friend Felix, who also has terminal cancer, and visits a clinic once a week to get his medicine. Sam has a real voice, just the right one for a child his age. His story brought tears to my eyes.<br/><br/>What struck me the most about the story was Sam's family. They were a functional fam</span>
  <span id="freeText2039846109968791496" style="display:none">The 9-to-12 age group's answer to Jenny Downham's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1314332.Before_I_Die" title="Before I Die by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Die</a>. 11-year-old Sam keeps a notebook in the final months of his life, while he's getting palliative care for his leukemia. He's on homebound instruction with his friend Felix, who also has terminal cancer, and visits a clinic once a week to get his medicine. Sam has a real voice, just the right one for a child his age. His story brought tears to my eyes.<br /><br />What struck me the most about the story was Sam's family. They were a functional family, refreshing to see when children's and young adult books are so full of decidedly DYSfunctional ones. Obviously his parents and sister were stressed from his illness, and they fought with each other about it, but it was clear that they all loved Sam very much and wanted him to be happy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2039846109968791496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Deanna Day" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1676348-deanna-day"><img alt="Deanna Day" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1255047278p2/1676348.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText11226046420736667603" style="display:none">Realistic fiction--death, family, writing, friendship, inquiring. <div id="review_1660328404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1660328404" />
    <a title="Courtney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19203783-courtney"><img alt="Courtney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454912500p2/19203783.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1660328404?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney" href="/user/show/19203783-courtney">Courtney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545069496" href="/book/show/8535885-ways-to-live-forever">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19203783-courtney?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1660328404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18274144386095937022">I got this book at my local bookstore on Independent Bookstore day. It was one of those "blind date" books where they wrap the book in paper and write a short description of the story on front, preventing you from "judging a book by its cover". I'm so glad that not only did I get this book but I couldn't see its cover- which doesn't relate the story at ALL and probably wouldn't have been a book I picked up on my own.<br/><br/>This story is told in a mix of letters, lists and journal entries. Ways to Live </span>
  <span id="freeText18274144386095937022" style="display:none">I got this book at my local bookstore on Independent Bookstore day. It was one of those "blind date" books where they wrap the book in paper and write a short description of the story on front, preventing you from "judging a book by its cover". I'm so glad that not only did I get this book but I couldn't see its cover- which doesn't relate the story at ALL and probably wouldn't have been a book I picked up on my own.<br /><br />This story is told in a mix of letters, lists and journal entries. Ways to Live forever, by Sally Nichols is narriated by an eleven year old boy named Sam who has Leukemia. There are also added pictures of drawings, ticket stubs and postcards- which complement this story so well. This story is fast paced and the language is very easy to read, but the story- oh the story. <br /><br />I don't know if I've ever been this emotional over such a short book, or any book to be honest. In just a short 224 pgs I had to put this book down countless times because of how emotionally gripping it is. <br /><br />While this novel isn't perfect, I rated it 5*'s because of how moving it is. If I was any less moved by this story I probably would've given it a solid 4*'s. I loved all the characters, although I wish there was a little more background info on them. Sam and Felix have a beautiful friendship and I absolutely love them both. There were some things I wish that could've been added to the story, minor details, that I feel would've made this story better/ stronger? <br /><br />This is small book packed with a powerful story and I'm left with mixed feelings. I'm heartbroken but relieved. I'm all over the place right now. So I'll be back to finish / fix my review tomorrow when my head is more clear. <br /><br />*** Edit *** <br /><br />I think why this book moved me so much is because I am a mother and I can't imagine being a parent to child with any sort of cancer or terminal illness. Sam's parents dealt with his disease in their own way, while struggling to keep him and themselves happy, healthy and stable. The strength these parents have... Its both incredible and inspiring. A cousin of mine just had to experience going through a kidney transplant surgery for her Adoptive son. What a scary situation. <br /><br />I did find things that I didn't like about the writting (lack of background info for one) but its such a beautiful story about such an ugly disease, that I'm keeping my rating at 5*'s. <br /><br />I definitely recommend this book to everyone. It could very well break your heart like it did mine, but its well worth the read. <br /><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="18274144386095937022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2057810806?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="enqi ☁️✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="enqi ☁️✨" href="/user/show/41427900-enqi">enqi ☁️✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2057810806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10830730476113195111"><blockquote> <i> List No 1: Five Facts About Me<br/>1. My name is Sam.<br/>2. I am eleven years old.<br/>3. I collect stories and fantastic facts.<br/>4. I have leukaemia.<br/>5. By the time you read this, I will probably be dead. </i> </blockquote><br/><br/>Reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2164318.Ways_to_Live_Forever' title='Ways to Live Forever by Sally Nicholls' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ways to Live Forever</a> was like a trainwreck. <br/><br/>I could see the end coming. With every page I turned I knew I was closer and closer to heartbreak. I think what made this book so gripping, so heartwarming yet so haunting, was how deceptively light it was. At first glance, it's just like any ordinary chil</span>
  <span id="freeText10830730476113195111" style="display:none"><blockquote> <i> List No 1: Five Facts About Me<br />1. My name is Sam.<br />2. I am eleven years old.<br />3. I collect stories and fantastic facts.<br />4. I have leukaemia.<br />5. By the time you read this, I will probably be dead. </i> </blockquote><br /><br />Reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2164318.Ways_to_Live_Forever" title="Ways to Live Forever by Sally Nicholls" rel="nofollow noopener">Ways to Live Forever</a> was like a trainwreck. <br /><br />I could see the end coming. With every page I turned I knew I was closer and closer to heartbreak. I think what made this book so gripping, so heartwarming yet so haunting, was how deceptively light it was. At first glance, it's just like any ordinary child's diary, filled with innocent musings and even a few messy drawings. But then you realise that in reality, the book is chillingly sombre as Sam comes to realise that his death may occur any time soon.<br /><br />The thing is, reading about the death of a child is never easy. Children are such carefree, joyful, naïve souls, and one can never believe that even they are taken from us too soon because they do not deserve it. Reading about it never gets easier. It didn't get easier for me. I never found it any easier to stomach Sam's impending death on the last page than I did the first page.<br /><br />I was completely fine at first. I really was. But I couldn't help but feel this sharp pang of sadness when Sam's best friend, Felix died, and I had to force my sob back when the diary abruptly ended a few days later, only to conclude with an entry that stated Sam had died painlessly and peacefully in his sleep. For a book targeted at a young audience, this book handled the subject of death and dying with a surprising delicacy. I won't be forgetting it any time soon. Please, if you have a few hours to spare and you're agonising over your next book - read this.<br /><br /><i> *Actual rating closer to 3.5 stars </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10830730476113195111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_52511692" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52511692" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/271355-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363406354p2/271355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52511692?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/271355-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545069489" href="/book/show/3192561-ways-to-live-forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/271355-jess?shelf=juv">juv</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52511692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6742226772357686209">Although I was personally caught up in Sam's story (and yes, crying through the second half), I was distracted by the question of whether or not this book would really appeal to an eleven year old boy. I know there's an appetite for sob-stories in young girls, but would boys pick this up? I can't say I know the answer, but one thing consoled me - Sam is really thinking things through. We see his distraught parents trying to cope, and occasionally they come on the scene as realistic, fully-fleshe</span>
  <span id="freeText6742226772357686209" style="display:none">Although I was personally caught up in Sam's story (and yes, crying through the second half), I was distracted by the question of whether or not this book would really appeal to an eleven year old boy. I know there's an appetite for sob-stories in young girls, but would boys pick this up? I can't say I know the answer, but one thing consoled me - Sam is really thinking things through. We see his distraught parents trying to cope, and occasionally they come on the scene as realistic, fully-fleshed characters, but Sam isn't thinking about his approaching death the way they are (although for the first time in a story like this, I found myself identifying with the parents - maybe because Sam is only 11). He's thinking about whether he could accomplish his goals (I loved the going up the down escalator scene) and what death is really like and how his book will end. <br /><br />Sam has a fantastic teacher who visits him at home - a personality mainly revealed to us through the experiments and projects she gives Sam - and up until the end she encourages Sam's scientific thinking and intellectual exploration. Since we know Sam is dying, this is a depiction of learning for its own sake (and not because it will be useful when you grow up) that could really inspire kids. Not in a maudlin "be grateful you have your health" way, or an "if a dying kid is this interested in science, you can be, too" way, but just showing the rewards of using your brain for whatever pursuits interest you. Which is all a long way of saying that the character development makes this more than just a sad, dying child story. Kids who like to ask those big questions will find it compelling. The rest of us might need some Kleenex handy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6742226772357686209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The language is simply but absolutely beautiful; portraits as well; it's really impossible not to love Felix and entire Sam's family (and of course Sam).   <span id="freeText7520594484761526098" style="display:none">How lovely novel this is. Normally I don't read novel for young adults but I did liked this one very much indeed. The language is simply but absolutely beautiful; portraits as well; it's really impossible not to love Felix and entire Sam's family (and of course Sam). From the very beginning you are stunned by horrifying circumstance characters of the novel are facing with and feel gratefulness cause you're not from that story. Then you realize that there are numerous people in precisely the same situation and from that moment you're not looking on this novel as a work of fiction. You're starting to feel their pain and respect their courage. You're seeing real children and their loved ones under those pages ...<br />Eventually you're absolutely emotionally attached with them so don't be surprise if your eyes start watering (be surprise if they don't!).</span>

<div id="review_747065064" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/24055107-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer747065064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5636872207805614891">I wonder what its like when you die? In this Realistic Fiction novel we will learn about how it might feel to die. I really loved how Sally Nicholls wrote the novel, because she made me feel like i was in the book and i was watching all the story and and there's parts where Sam would stop and say what he would be thinking about that thing. I liked that she wrote in like a diary which made it kinda cool because she would write like on March 22 and the next chapter would be on April 15th. I liked </span>
  <span id="freeText5636872207805614891" style="display:none">I wonder what its like when you die? In this Realistic Fiction novel we will learn about how it might feel to die. I really loved how Sally Nicholls wrote the novel, because she made me feel like i was in the book and i was watching all the story and and there's parts where Sam would stop and say what he would be thinking about that thing. I liked that she wrote in like a diary which made it kinda cool because she would write like on March 22 and the next chapter would be on April 15th. I liked the book because it was short and a easy book for me.<br /> <br /> Ways to Live Forever is about a boy named Sam and he has and illness and while hes in the hospital he meets a boy named Felix and they become best friends and they got home-schooled and Mrs.Willis they would do experiments that would blow-up things n the house. Sam had a little sister named Ella and she thought it was unfair that Sam didn't have to go to school and she did, but what she didn't understand was that Sam couldn't go to school because he would get very tired and something could happen, Sam got ill, like two or three time but then Sam gets worse. The setting is at Sams house and at the hospital. Since Sam got ill he he couldn't run and do everything everybody did for example he couldn't run , walk alot and he wanted to be cured. Ways to Live Forever was Person vs Self because Sams family was sad and frustrated because he took alot of medicine that didn't even help at all. Sam collects information about aliens spaceships because he wants to be a scientist, Ella is his sister and she doesn't get that her brother is ill and that's why he gets a different treatment from her parents than she does. Mom is worried about Sam that he might get worse and so does dad think that.<br /><br /> I was angry when Sam's dad didn't let Sam go sledging just because supposedly he could get hurt. "I don't think that people can get hurt with snow going sledging." I was surprised when Mom let Ella miss school to go sledging even though Dad said they couldn't go sledging. "I would also miss school because we don't get that much of snow very often." A theme that I think its the books theme is bravery and faith because Sam's family has to be brave when Sam got ill, and they all need to have faith in order for Sam to get better from his illness. I wish the author didn't make Dad very strict because it makes the book lamer than people might think. This book is similar to The Running Dream and Heart to Heart because both stories have something kind off bad for the characters for example Jessica (in The Running Dream) lost one of her legs and she has a hard time getting back on track and Kasey has also a hard time because her best friend passed away and Sam has a hard time facing his illness problems and everyday he discovers new ones and its hard for him. Ways to Live Forever has a relation to my life because i used to have the illness similar to Sam but luckily up okay now.<br /><br /> In conclusion, I think it was a well written book because I was able to understand the book and for me it was easy to read and now ita one of my favorite books. I rate this book a 9 out of 10 because it was written in like a diary or a letter and im not a really big fan of that, but i did like the book over all. I recommend this book to anyone who likes young adult novels and to anyone else too. If you still don't know how it might feel to die then you should read Ways to Live Forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5636872207805614891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10790418210161165556" style="display:none">***Spoiler Alert***<br />Do you know someone who wrote a book about your death? Well in this book a boy named Sam writes about events leading to his death. Sam is an eleven year old boy that has leukemia. Sam wants to live his last few days with his family and friends. The genre of this book is realistic fiction. I think this book is a very sad book but a very good one as well.<br /><br />This book takes place in Sams home town. Sam wants to live his lasts moments with his friends and family but his time living is almost over so he wants to do whatever he wants so he could be happy,then that way he doesn't have to be sad or think about his time left living. This type of conflict is person vs. self because Sam has to fight his sickness so he could be able to live crazy and wild instead of being in a hospital and sad. Sams mom is worried about Sams sickness and just wants to think that nothing is going to happen. Sams Dad is serious and complicated in the beginning but then at the end he starts being kind and happy. Felix's Sam's best friend is wild,crazy,and also sick but he has Cancer. Ella Sam's sister is crazy,nice, and sweet. Sam is creative,nice, shy,outgoing,intelligent,and emotional cause of all the things that happen he still has a positive mood. Then I closed my eyes again and drifted back into sleep". I was moved when dad told Sam that he had dreamt about him. In the text is states, "But then--- About you he said. I turned my face toward him. He was quiet again. You,he said. Going Away......". The main character Sams problem was that he was going to die. In the text it states, "Sam died quietly in his sleep. I believe this book is the same as Mockingbird because they both talk about people dying so that makes them be the same. This book reminds me of my aunts sisters brother because he has leukemia and he also died of this illness. Also this illness causes a lot of sadness to people. <br /><br />I believe this book was amazing! I love this book and it also made me cry a little at the end. I rate this book a 10 because it was a great book and I hope that other people will like it as well. I would recommend this book to anyone not anyone in particular cause it was a great book and I don't think specific people have to read it so that's why I say anyone can. <div id="review_1421377650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1421377650" />
    <a title="Suze Lavender" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29148122-suze-lavender"><img alt="Suze Lavender" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492887152p2/29148122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1421377650?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suze Lavender" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suze Lavender" href="/user/show/29148122-suze-lavender">Suze Lavender</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1421377650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16300293507608979052">Sam is eleven years old. He likes lists, records and facts, he has a sister called Ella and a friend called Felix. Sam has leukemia and he has a list of things he still wants to do in his life. He's writing a book about everything that occupies his mind. He has a lot of questions and tries to find the answers. He wonders about death, dying and being dead, but also about living. He wants to kiss a girl, fly in an airship, drink alcohol, etc. Sam tries to make the most of the time he has left...<br/><br/>Sa</span>
  <span id="freeText16300293507608979052" style="display:none">Sam is eleven years old. He likes lists, records and facts, he has a sister called Ella and a friend called Felix. Sam has leukemia and he has a list of things he still wants to do in his life. He's writing a book about everything that occupies his mind. He has a lot of questions and tries to find the answers. He wonders about death, dying and being dead, but also about living. He wants to kiss a girl, fly in an airship, drink alcohol, etc. Sam tries to make the most of the time he has left...<br /><br />Sam is such a special kid with a brilliant mind, which immediately made me like him a lot. I loved how Sally Nicholls lets him answer his own questions. There are several daring ones, things that I think a lot of people want answers to, but are afraid to ask. The topics are all well chosen and the book is so beautifully written. I shed a lot of tears, but also smiled. It's obvious from the beginning that Sam isn't going to get better, but his legacy is precious. He lives forever on paper. Even though he's a fictional character he could have been real. That's what makes the story come so close and that is what makes this book really good.<br /><br />Sam likes facts and this book is informative as well as moving. It's a great combination. Sam's matter of fact way of dealing with important questions and issues makes the story even better. He's dying, but he's tough. He's got such an admirable personality and still he's also an eleven year old with wishes and dreams that are normal for his age. I liked that balance and think it made the story really strong. Sally Nicholls also doesn't forget to show her readers what it's like for siblings and parents to live with a loved one who's terribly ill. Even though it isn't long the story is complete. I think Ways to Live Forever is impressive and gripping, it's a story that touches your heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16300293507608979052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_862677450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/862677450" />
    <a title="Michele" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3983777-michele"><img alt="Michele" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352008504p2/3983777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/862677450?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michele" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michele" href="/user/show/3983777-michele">Michele</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545069489" href="/book/show/3192561-ways-to-live-forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3983777-michele?shelf=childrens-chapter">childrens-chapter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3983777-michele?shelf=caudill">caudill</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3983777-michele?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer862677450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1277193966847695763">In general, I am not a fan of books which are primarily <i>sad</i>. I do not mean tragedy—I enjoy those well enough—I mean stories of illness, depression, pain, death. It is not that I do not have an appreciation for these stories…I just do not enjoy being sad. <br/><br/>Ways to Live Forever is sad. It is about a tweenage boy who is dying of Leukemia. There isn’t much doubt that he is dying. The story begins when his family has basically been told that there is nothing more to do for him, and he has months left </span>
  <span id="freeText1277193966847695763" style="display:none">In general, I am not a fan of books which are primarily <i>sad</i>. I do not mean tragedy—I enjoy those well enough—I mean stories of illness, depression, pain, death. It is not that I do not have an appreciation for these stories…I just do not enjoy being sad. <br /><br />Ways to Live Forever is sad. It is about a tweenage boy who is dying of Leukemia. There isn’t much doubt that he is dying. The story begins when his family has basically been told that there is nothing more to do for him, and he has months left to live. Sam is pretty matter-of-fact about his impending death, but is somewhat bothered by the things he has not gotten to do, like kiss or a girl or drink alcohol. <br /><br />Most of this quiet story is about Sam writing a book about the questions he has and the things he wants to do with his life before he dies. The rest of it is about he and his friend (who also has cancer) trying to do as much as they can from his list, while dealing with the reactions of Sam’s doctors, teacher, sister, and parents. <br /><br />This book is sad and beautiful. It is also funny. Sam's goals are so simple they are funny--he wants to walk UP the down escalator, but he is deeply worried about being caught. There is something joyful about this book, despite its prevalent cloud of death. Sam’s journal is all about the wonder and celebration of Sam’s life. This book has been very popular among my 4th and 5th grade students, and several of them have asked if this is a true story. It <i>feels</i> like a true story, but I believe that is just because the author did her research and based her character on what life is like for actual cancer victims. <br /><br />I highly recommend this book, but there is not getting around the fact that it is a sad book. Enjoy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1277193966847695763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24059900-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388842090p2/24059900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/749191712?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/24059900-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer749191712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8234706467308136035"> What do you think happens when you die? Does it hurt? Do you go heaven?<br/>In this realistic fiction a boy may have to face that sometime soon. I loved reading this book its funny and sad but reading this makes you think throughout the whole book like *** Spoiler Alert *** Sam has leukemia and on a wish list he wants to do teenage things like smoke and get girls so his friend Felix gives him a cigarette. I was like wait a minute why would he want to do that when he is sick because that for sure is </span>
  <span id="freeText8234706467308136035" style="display:none"> What do you think happens when you die? Does it hurt? Do you go heaven?<br />In this realistic fiction a boy may have to face that sometime soon. I loved reading this book its funny and sad but reading this makes you think throughout the whole book like *** Spoiler Alert *** Sam has leukemia and on a wish list he wants to do teenage things like smoke and get girls so his friend Felix gives him a cigarette. I was like wait a minute why would he want to do that when he is sick because that for sure is not going to help you get better but make you worse.<br /><br />Sam is boy who is very sick and he wants to make a list and tell his story about battling something difficult with his friend Felix but something bad happens and he has to make the list on his own so he gets to making the list then he finally finishes the list and and answers his questions truthfully. The setting was in there neigborhood, the hospital, and his house. Person V.s person because Sam and his friend Felix have totally opposite personality's and Sam tries hard to go along with Felix but doesn't always wants to but does it because Felix is his friend.<br /><br />This was an amazing book! I loved every part of this book it really caught my attention. It makes you laugh and it makes you cry. This book would be great for people who like emotionally funny books.<br /><br />Overall this book was amazing i give it a perfect 10 everything about it just made me fall in love with it. I loved it soo much. It made me realize to be happy for what i got and be happy with who i am because you never know what can happen.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183820095" />
    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2042050-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315891241p2/2042050.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183820095?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/2042050-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545069489" href="/book/show/3192561-ways-to-live-forever">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183820095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16815576930706386017">This is an incredible book told from the first person point of view by Sam, an 11 year old boy dying of leukemia. Wow.....<br/><br/>This is not the typical type of book I read, but I read this book because my daughter started it and continued to give me updates about Sam and Felix (Sams friend), and some of the "updates" were getting a little heavy, so I decided to read it myself. I was not disappointed. You, will not be disappointed! It also opened a door for my daughter and I to discuss things we wouldn</span>
  <span id="freeText16815576930706386017" style="display:none">This is an incredible book told from the first person point of view by Sam, an 11 year old boy dying of leukemia. Wow.....<br /><br />This is not the typical type of book I read, but I read this book because my daughter started it and continued to give me updates about Sam and Felix (Sams friend), and some of the "updates" were getting a little heavy, so I decided to read it myself. I was not disappointed. You, will not be disappointed! It also opened a door for my daughter and I to discuss things we wouldn't normally talk about.<br /><br />You can't help but fall in love with Sam. He is so full of life and has so many aspirations at 11 years old, that you really feel like you know him. You go through his trials and jubilations and feel as if you are personally there, experiencing things with him. <br /><br />I will warn you now, there are lots of tears to be cried during the reading of Sams story. Just when I felt like I was over it and okay again, the author adds a little something and there you go.... again.<br />I am definitely glad that I got to know Sam and hear his story, despite the emotional ride that I went on.<br /><br />This a great book, and meeting Sam and learning about his dreams and aspirations and seeing how he set out to achieve things all while dealing with leukemia makes me wonder what we could all accomplish with a little more Sam attitude.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16815576930706386017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1117212182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1117212182" />
    <a title="Paula  Phillips" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1969584-paula-phillips"><img alt="Paula  Phillips" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574564336p2/1969584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1117212182?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula  Phillips" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula  Phillips" href="/user/show/1969584-paula-phillips">Paula  Phillips</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1117212182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6724855433534293152"> With the movie and book "The Fault in Our Stars" released, the teens of nowadays are going through a phase of reading books that are set around the topic of "Cancer". When you get to my age though, you have read so many books about this topic, that often it can get kind of boring as you are reading the same thing over and over again. However, Sally Nicholls book "Ways to Live Forever" was amazing and was definitely not boring. The book is set around two main characters 11 year old Sam and 13 ye</span>
  <span id="freeText6724855433534293152" style="display:none"> With the movie and book "The Fault in Our Stars" released, the teens of nowadays are going through a phase of reading books that are set around the topic of "Cancer". When you get to my age though, you have read so many books about this topic, that often it can get kind of boring as you are reading the same thing over and over again. However, Sally Nicholls book "Ways to Live Forever" was amazing and was definitely not boring. The book is set around two main characters 11 year old Sam and 13 year old Felix . Both of the boys have Cancer and are dying, so they are home-schooled by Mrs Willis. One day Mrs Willis gives the boys an idea - to write a book . Sam gets really into it and starts to make a bucket list and a book filled with random questions about Cancer, Death and the actual Dying part and begins writing. Felix , the more outgoing one decides to help Sam tick off and complete his bucket list one by one. The book not only focuses on Sam and Felix but also their families reaction to the Cancer issue. Ways to Live Forever was a really good read and it was great to see Tween/Teen Male Protagonists for a change as well. I will warn you readers that be prepared for the ending with the mindset that it is a "cancer story".<br />This book is really worth reading and fans of "The Fault in Our Stars" will enjoy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6724855433534293152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1129092374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1129092374" />
    <a title="Ann-Marie  Ng" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17298442-ann-marie-ng"><img alt="Ann-Marie  Ng" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129092374?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann-Marie  Ng" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann-Marie  Ng" href="/user/show/17298442-ann-marie-ng">Ann-Marie  Ng</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129092374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5715047244979945808">Compared to The Fault in Our Stars, this was the better cancer book. <br/><br/>There was no profound monologues, over dramatic scenes or wild romance. There was just an eleven year old boy named Sam and his family and his friend Felix. While living life at home, Sam sometimes goes to do some of the things in his half baked to-do list, has some time with family and friends, and ponders together with Felix "How do you know you are dead" and where do people go after they die" the answers, which he compiles i</span>
  <span id="freeText5715047244979945808" style="display:none">Compared to The Fault in Our Stars, this was the better cancer book. <br /><br />There was no profound monologues, over dramatic scenes or wild romance. There was just an eleven year old boy named Sam and his family and his friend Felix. While living life at home, Sam sometimes goes to do some of the things in his half baked to-do list, has some time with family and friends, and ponders together with Felix "How do you know you are dead" and where do people go after they die" the answers, which he compiles into a list, are hilarious btw. <br /><br />Maybe people might find TFIOS more moving and dramatic. But this I found more moving in its own quieter way. Everyone went for the more light-hearted moments in life and humour when they could, without any angst whatsover. The biggest difference was that no one treated themselves so seriously. Maybe I don't want to feel more depressed and be bummed out after reading something. Maybe out of this genre, I want something bittersweet but yet inspires others to live doing what they can. Somthing like this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5715047244979945808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DMblX/o0Mat6HvE++YQO4DYzzKuAd2brhwqlklaxFqm1AHQzJr1EOD6j/WeMl6LCHQR4LtZrswiRQpzK+lSwSg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer13728825481892407084"> Sally Nicholls is a prize-winning British children's author. She was born and grew up in Stockton-on-Tees. On finishing school, Nicholls chose to travel around the world. Her first novel was Ways to Live Forever.</span>
